--- Planning Phase (Iteration 1/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
Let me analyze this theorem step-by-step.

**Goal**: Prove that if `w` has period `p` and `u` is a prefix of `w` with length at least `p`, then `u` also has period `p`.

**Understanding the setup**:

From `CoW/Period.lean`:
```lean
def HasPeriod (w : Word α) (p : ℕ) : Prop :=
  0 < p ∧ ∀ i : ℕ, i + p < w.length → w.get? i = w.get? (i + p)
```

From `CoW/Factor.lean`:
```lean
def IsPrefix (u w : Word α) : Prop := List.IsPrefix u w
lemma IsPrefix.def (u w : Word α) : (u ≤ₚ w) ↔ ∃ v, w = u ++ v
```

**What we have**:
- `hp : HasPeriod w p`, so:
  - `0 < p`
  - `∀ i, i + p < w.length → w.get? i = w.get? (i + p)`
- `hpre : u ≤ₚ w`, so there exists `v` with `w = u ++ v`
- `hlen : p ≤ u.length`

**What we need to show**:
- `HasPeriod u p`, which means:
  - `0 < p` ✓ (directly from `hp.1`)
  - `∀ i, i + p < u.length → u.get? i = u.get? (i + p)`

**Key insight**:

Since `u` is a prefix of `w`, we have `w = u ++ v` for some `v`.

For any index `i < u.length`, accessing `w[i]` gives `u[i]` (accessing the prefix part).

For the period property:
- Take any `i` with `i + p < u.length`
- Since `u.length ≤ w.length` (from prefix property), we have `i + p < w.length`
- From `hp.2`: `w.get? i = w.get? (i + p)`
- Since both `i < u.length` and `i + p < u.length` (from assumption), both indices access the prefix `u`
- So `u.get? i = w.get? i = w.get? (i + p) = u.get? (i + p)`

**Proof strategy**:

1. **Show `0 < p`**: Direct from `hp.1`

2. **Show periodicity for `u`**:
   - Extract the decomposition: `w = u ++ v` from `hpre`
   - For any `i` with `i + p < u.length`:
     - Show `i < w.length` and `i + p < w.length` (both follow from `i + p < u.length ≤ w.length`)
     - Use `hp.2` to get `w.get? i = w.get? (i + p)`
     - Show `u.get? i = w.get? i` (because `i < u.length` and `w = u ++ v`)
     - Show `u.get? (i + p) = w.get? (i + p)` (because `i + p < u.length` and `w = u ++ v`)
     - Combine by transitivity

**Technical details for `get?` on prefixes**:

When `w = u ++ v` and `i < u.length`:
- `w.get? i = (u ++ v).get? i = u.get? i`
- This uses `List.get?_append` or `List.getElem?_append_left`

```lean
obtain ⟨v, hw⟩ := (IsPrefix.def u w).mp hpre
refine ⟨hp.1, fun i hi => ?_⟩
calc u.get? i 
    = (u ++ v).get? i := by 
        symm
        exact List.getElem?_append_left (by omega : i < u.length)
  _ = w.get? i := by rw [← hw]
  _ = w.get? (i + p) := hp.2 i (by
        have : u.length ≤ w.length := IsPrefix.length_le hpre
        omega)
  _ = (u ++ v).get? (i + p) := by rw [hw]
  _ = u.get? (i + p) := List.getElem?_append_left (by omega : i + p < u.length)
```

**Key lemma to reference**:
- `List.getElem?_append_left` (from Mathlib): 
  `(l ++ l').getElem? n = l.getElem? n` when `n < l.length`

This is the crucial lemma. If this doesn't exist with this exact name, we might need `List.get?_append_left` or similar.

**Recommended final proof**:

```lean
obtain ⟨v, hw⟩ := (IsPrefix.def u w).mp hpre
refine ⟨hp.1, fun i hi => ?_⟩
have hi_bound : i < u.length := by omega
have hip_bound : i + p < u.length := hi  
have hi_w : i + p < w.length := by
  calc i + p < u.length := hi
       _ ≤ w.length := IsPrefix.length_le hpre
calc u.get? i
    = (u ++ v).get? i := (List.getElem?_append_left hi_bound).symm
  _ = w.get? i := by rw [← hw]
  _ = w.get? (i + p) := hp.2 i hi_w
  _ = (u ++ v).get? (i + p) := by rw [hw]
  _ = u.get? (i + p) := List.getElem?_append_left hip_bound
```

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
Let me analyze this theorem step-by-step.

**Goal**: Prove that `w ^ (n + 1)` has period `w.length` for any non-empty `w` and any `n`.

**Understanding the setup**:

From `CoW/Period.lean`:
```lean
def HasPeriod (w : Word α) (p : ℕ) : Prop :=
  0 < p ∧ ∀ i : ℕ, i + p < w.length → w.get? i = w.get? (i + p)
```

From `CoW/Word.lean`:
```lean
lemma Word.pow_succ (w : Word α) (n : ℕ) : w ^ (n + 1) = w ^ n ⬝ w
lemma Word.length_pow (w : Word α) (n : ℕ) : (w ^ n).length = n * w.length
```

**What we need to show**:
- `HasPeriod (w ^ (n + 1)) w.length`, which means:
  - `0 < w.length` (w is non-empty)
  - For all `i`, if `i + w.length < (w ^ (n + 1)).length`, then `(w ^ (n + 1)).get? i = (w ^ (n + 1)).get? (i + w.length)`

**Key observations**:

1. `(w ^ (n + 1)).length = (n + 1) * w.length` (by `Word.length_pow`)

2. The condition `i + w.length < (n + 1) * w.length` simplifies to `i < n * w.length`

3. The word `w ^ (n + 1)` is `w` repeated `n + 1` times:
   - `w ^ (n + 1) = w ⬝ w ⬝ ... ⬝ w` (`n + 1` copies)

4. For any position `i` in `w ^ (n + 1)`, the character at position `i` and position `i + w.length` come from consecutive copies of `w`, so they access the same position within `w`.

**More precisely**:

If we think of `w ^ (n + 1)` as positions `0, 1, ..., (n+1)*w.length - 1`:
- Position `i` is in the `k`-th copy of `w` where `k = i / w.length`, at local position `i mod w.length`
- Position `i + w.length` is in the `(k+1)`-th copy of `w`, at the same local position `i mod w.length`

So both positions access the same character from `w`.

**Proof strategy**:

This is very similar to the `hasPeriod_concat_self` theorem, but generalized to `n+1` copies instead of 2.

**Approach 1: Induction on n**:

- **Base case** `n = 0`: 
  - `w ^ 1 = w`, need to show `HasPeriod w w.length`
  - But this is vacuous! If `i + w.length < w.length`, then `i < 0`, which is impossible.
  - So the periodicity condition is trivially true (empty universal quantification)

- **Inductive step** `n → n + 1`:
  - IH: `HasPeriod (w ^ (n + 1)) w.length`
  - Goal: `HasPeriod (w ^ (n + 2)) w.length`
  - We have `w ^ (n + 2) = w ^ (n + 1) ⬝ w`
  - This is similar to the concat case

**Approach 2: Direct proof using the structure**:

For any `i` with `i + w.length < (w ^ (n + 1)).length`:
- Let `k = i / w.length` and `r = i mod w.length`
- Then `i = k * w.length + r` where `0 ≤ r < w.length`
- Position `i` in `w ^ (n + 1)` accesses `w[r]`
- Position `i + w.length = (k + 1) * w.length + r` accesses `w[r]` from the next copy
- So they're equal

But this requires working with division and modular arithmetic, which might be complex.

**Approach 3: Use existing lemma**:

We already have (or should have) `hasPeriod_concat_self` which shows `w ⬝ w` has period `w.length`.

Can we use this? Well, `w ^ 2 = w ⬝ w`, so `w ^ 2` has period `w.length`.

For `w ^ 3 = w ^ 2 ⬝ w = (w ⬝ w) ⬝ w`, we might need to show that concatenating another copy preserves the period.

Actually, there might be a general lemma: if `u` has period `p` and `v` starts the same way (in some sense), then `u ⬝ v` has period `p`.

But this is getting complex. Let me think of the simplest approach.

**Simplest approach: Show it's a special case of a general pattern**:

Actually, for `w ^ (n + 1)`, we can think of it as `w ⬝ w ^ n`.

If we can show that for any suffix that "aligns" with the period, concatenation preserves the period, we'd be done.

But let me just suggest a direct proof by working with the indices.

No specific plan block detected.

- Position `i + w.length` falls in the next copy of `w`, at the same local position
- So they access the same character

**Goal**: Prove `HasPeriod (w ^ (n + 1)) w.length` given `hw : w ≠ []`.

**Step-by-step**:

1. **Prove `0 < w.length`**: 
   ```lean
   exact List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil.mpr hw
   ```

2. **Prove periodicity by induction on n**:

   **Rewrite the goal first**:
   ```lean
   rw [Word.pow_succ]  -- w ^ (n + 1) = w ^ n ⬝ w
   ```

   Now we need to prove `HasPeriod (w ^ n ⬝ w) w.length`.

   **Case analysis on n**:
   
   - **Case `n = 0`**: 
     - `w ^ 0 ⬝ w = [] ⬝ w = w`
     - Need `HasPeriod w w.length`
     - This is vacuous (no valid `i` with `i + w.length < w.length`)
   
   - **Case `n ≥ 1`**:
     - We have `w ^ n ⬝ w` where `n ≥ 1`
     - Length is `n * w.length + w.length = (n + 1) * w.length`
     
     For any `i` with `i + w.length < (n + 1) * w.length`:
     
     **Split into cases**:
     
     a. If `i + w.length ≤ n * w.length`:
        - Both `i` and `i + w.length` are in the `w ^ n` part
        - By IH, `w ^ n` has period `w.length`
        - So `(w ^ n)[i] = (w ^ n)[i + w.length]`
        - Access in `w ^ n ⬝ w` gives the same
     
     b. If `i < n * w.length` and `i + w.length > n * w.length`:
        - `i` is in `w ^ n` part, `i + w.length` is in the final `w` part
        - Need to show they're equal
        - This requires showing that `w ^ n` and `w` "align" properly

Actually, case (b) is the tricky part. Let me think about this more carefully.

When `i < n * w.length ≤ i + w.length`:
- We have `n * w.length - i ≤ w.length`
- Position `i` in `w ^ n` is at local position `i mod w.length` in some copy of `w`
- Position `i + w.length` wraps into the final `w`, at position `(i + w.length) - n * w.length`
- We need: `(w ^ n)[i] = w[(i + w.length) - n * w.length]`

Hmm, this still requires showing alignment.

**Completely different approach**: Prove it directly without induction by showing the modular structure.

**Helper Lemma**: For any `k` positions in `w ^ (n+1)` that differ by `w.length`, they access the same position modulo `w.length` in `w`.

Then the period property follows immediately.

```lean4
refine ⟨List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil.mpr hw, ?_⟩
intro i hi
-- We'll use induction on n
induction n generalizing i with
| zero =>
  -- w ^ 1 = w, so i + w.length < w.length is impossible
  have : (w ^ 1).length = w.length := by simp [Word.length_pow]
  rw [this] at hi
  omega
| succ n ih =>
  -- w ^ (n + 2) = w ^ (n + 1) ⬝ w
  have eq_pow : w ^ (n + 1 + 1) = w ^ (n + 1) ⬝ w := by
    rw [Word.pow_succ]
  rw [eq_pow] at hi ⊢
  have hlen : (w ^ (n + 1)).length = (n + 1) * w.length := Word.length_pow w (n + 1)
  have hlen_total : (w ^ (n + 1) ⬝ w).length = (n + 1) * w.length + w.length := by
    simp [Word.length_concat, hlen]
  -- Case split based on where i and i + w.length fall
  by_cases hi_in_prefix : i + w.length < (w ^ (n + 1)).length
  · -- Both i and i + w.length are in w ^ (n + 1)
    have get_i : ((w ^ (n + 1)) ++ w).get? i = (w ^ (n + 1)).get? i := 
      List.getElem?_append_left (by omega : i < (w ^ (n + 1)).length)
    have get_i_plus : ((w ^ (n + 1)) ++ w).get? (i + w.length) = (w ^ (n + 1)).get? (i + w.length) := 
      List.getElem?_append_left hi_in_prefix
    rw [get_i, get_i_plus]
    exact ih i hi_in_prefix
  · -- i + w.length >= (w ^ (n + 1)).length
    push_neg at hi_in_prefix
    by_cases hi_self : i < (w ^ (n + 1)).length
    · -- i is in w ^ (n + 1), but i + w.length is in the final w
      have get_i : ((w ^ (n + 1)) ++ w).get? i = (w ^ (n + 1)).get? i := 
        List.getElem?_append_left hi_self
      have offset : i + w.length - (w ^ (n + 1)).length < w.length := by omega
      have get_i_plus : ((w ^ (n + 1)) ++ w).get? (i + w.length) = w.get? (i + w.length - (w ^ (n + 1)).length) := by
        rw [List.getElem?_append_right hi_in_prefix]
      rw [get_i, get_i_plus]
      -- Now we need: (w ^ (n + 1)).get? i = w.get? (i + w.length - (w ^ (n + 1)).length)
      -- Key insight: i and (i + w.length - (w ^ (n + 1)).length) differ by (w ^ (n + 1)).length - w.length = n * w.length
      have key_eq : i = (i + w.length - (w ^ (n + 1)).length) + ((w ^ (n + 1)).length - w.length) := by omega
      have mod_eq : (w ^ (n + 1)).length - w.length = n * w.length := by rw [hlen]; ring
      rw [key_eq, mod_eq]
      -- Now use that w^(n+1) has period w.length by IH
      have j := i + w.length - (w ^ (n + 1)).length
      have hj : j + n * w.length = i + w.length - (w ^ (n + 1)).length + n * w.length := rfl
      clear key_eq mod_eq hj
      -- Apply IH n times
      clear hi_in_prefix hi_self get_i get_i_plus offset eq_pow hlen_total hi
      induction n generalizing i with
      | zero => simp
      | succ m ihm =>
        have step : (i + w.length - (w ^ (m + 1 + 1)).length) + (m + 1) * w.length = 
                    ((i + w.length - (w ^ (m + 1 + 1)).length) + m * w.length) + w.length := by ring
        rw [step]
        have hlen_m : (w ^ (m + 1)).length = (m + 1) * w.length := Word.length_pow w (m + 1)
        have bound : (i + w.length - (w ^ (m + 1 + 1)).length) + m * w.length < (w ^ (m + 1)).length := by
          have : (w ^ (m + 1 + 1)).length = (w ^ (m + 1)).length + w.length := by
            rw [Word.pow_succ, Word.length_concat]
          omega
        rw [← ihm bound]
    · -- Both i and i + w.length are in the final w
      push_neg at hi_self
      have offset_i : i - (w ^ (n + 1)).length < w.length := by omega
      have offset_plus : i + w.length - (w ^ (n + 1)).length < w.length := by omega
      have get_i : ((w ^ (n + 1)) ++ w).get? i = w.get? (i - (w ^ (n + 1)).length) := 
        List.getElem?_append_right hi_self
      have get_i_plus : ((w ^ (n + 1)) ++ w).get? (i + w.length) = w.get? (i + w.length - (w ^ (n + 1)).length) := 
        List.getElem?_append_right (by omega : (w ^ (n + 1)).length ≤ i + w.length)
      rw [get_i, get_i_plus]
      congr 1
      omega
```

```lean4
refine ⟨List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil.mpr hw, ?_⟩
intro i hi
-- We'll use induction on n
induction n generalizing i with
| zero =>
  -- w ^ 1 = w, so i + w.length < w.length is impossible
  have : (w ^ 1).length = w.length := by simp [Word.length_pow]
  rw [this] at hi
  omega
| succ n ih =>
  -- w ^ (n + 2) = w ^ (n + 1) ⬝ w
  have eq_pow : w ^ (n + 1 + 1) = w ^ (n + 1) ⬝ w := by
    rw [Word.pow_succ]
  rw [eq_pow] at hi ⊢
  have hlen : (w ^ (n + 1)).length = (n + 1) * w.length := Word.length_pow w (n + 1)
  have hlen_total : (w ^ (n + 1) ⬝ w).length = (n + 1) * w.length + w.length := by
    simp [Word.length_concat, hlen]
  -- Case split based on where i and i + w.length fall
  by_cases hi_in_prefix : i + w.length < (w ^ (n + 1)).length
  · -- Both i and i + w.length are in w ^ (n + 1)
    have i_lt : i < (w ^ (n + 1)).length := by omega
    simp only [Word.concat, List.append_eq_append]
    rw [List.get?_append i_lt, List.get?_append hi_in_prefix]
    exact ih i hi_in_prefix
  · -- i + w.length >= (w ^ (n + 1)).length
    push_neg at hi_in_prefix
    by_cases hi_self : i < (w ^ (n + 1)).length
    · -- i is in w ^ (n + 1), but i + w.length is in the final w
      simp only [Word.concat, List.append_eq_append]
      rw [List.get?_append hi_self]
      have not_lt : ¬(i + w.length < (w ^ (n + 1)).length) := hi_in_prefix
      rw [List.get?_append_right not_lt]
      -- Now we need: (w ^ (n + 1)).get? i = w.get? (i + w.length - (w ^ (n + 1)).length)
      -- This requires showing the periodicity aligns
      have offset : i + w.length - (w ^ (n + 1)).length < w.length := by omega
      have key : i = (i + w.length - (w ^ (n + 1)).length) + ((w ^ (n + 1)).length - w.length) := by omega
      have len_diff : (w ^ (n + 1)).length - w.length = n * w.length := by rw [hlen]; ring
      rw [key, len_diff]
      clear key len_diff hi_in_prefix not_lt offset eq_pow hlen_total hi hi_self
      -- Apply periodicity n times
      generalize i + w.length - (w ^ (n + 1)).length = j
      intro
      clear i
      induction n generalizing j with
      | zero => simp
      | succ m ihm =>
        have hlen_m : (w ^ (m + 1)).length = (m + 1) * w.length := Word.length_pow w (m + 1)
        have step : j + (m + 1) * w.length = (j + m * w.length) + w.length := by ring
        rw [step]
        have bound : j + m * w.length < (w ^ (m + 1)).length := by
          have : (w ^ (m + 1 + 1)).length = (w ^ (m + 1)).length + w.length := by
            rw [Word.pow_succ, Word.length_concat]
          omega
        rw [← ihm bound]
    · -- Both i and i + w.length are in the final w
      push_neg at hi_self
      simp only [Word.concat, List.append_eq_append]
      rw [List.get?_append_right (le_of_not_lt hi_self)]
      rw [List.get?_append_right (by omega : (w ^ (n + 1)).length ≤ i + w.length)]
      congr 1
      omega
```

```lean
    (hi : i < (w ^ k).length) :
```

```lean
theorem hasPeriod_pow_length {w : Word α} (hw : w ≠ []) (n : ℕ) :
    HasPeriod (w ^ (n + 1)) w.length := by
  refine ⟨List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil.mpr hw, fun i hi => ?_⟩
  rw [get?_pow_eq_get?_mod (by omega) hw i (by omega)]
  rw [get?_pow_eq_get?_mod (by omega) hw (i + w.length) (by omega)]
  congr 1
  -- Now just need: i % w.length = (i + w.length) % w.length
  have : w.length > 0 := List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil.mpr hw
  exact Nat.add_mod_right i w.length
```

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
Let me analyze this theorem step-by-step.

**Goal**: Prove that the length of the morphism applied to `a :: u` equals the length of `f a` plus the length of the morphism applied to `u`.

**Understanding morphisms**:

From `CoW/Morphism.lean`:
```lean
def applyMorphism (f : α → Word β) (w : Word α) : Word β :=
  w.flatMap f

notation f " •w " w => applyMorphism f w
```

And we have:
```lean
@[simp]
lemma applyMorphism_concat (f : α → Word β) (u v : Word α) :
    f •w (u ⬝ v) = (f •w u) ⬝ (f •w v)
```

**What we need to show**:
`(f •w (a :: u)).length = (f a).length + (f •w u).length`

**Key observations**:

1. `a :: u` is the same as `[a] ++ u` in list notation
2. We can use the concat property of morphisms
3. Or we can use the definition of `flatMap` directly

**Approach 1: Use the concat lemma**

```lean
(f •w (a :: u)).length 
  = (f •w ([a] ++ u)).length          -- a :: u is [a] ++ u
  = (f •w [a] ⬝ f •w u).length        -- by applyMorphism_concat
  = (f •w [a]).length + (f •w u).length  -- by Word.length_concat
  = (f a).length + (f •w u).length    -- by applyMorphism_letter
```

**Approach 2: Use flatMap directly**

```lean
f •w (a :: u)
  = (a :: u).flatMap f                -- by definition
  = f a ++ u.flatMap f                -- by List.flatMap_cons
  = f a ++ (f •w u)                   -- by definition
```

Then the length follows by `List.length_append`.

**Approach 2 is simpler and more direct.**

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
**Goal**: Prove `(f •w (a :: u)).length = (f a).length + (f •w u).length`.

**Strategy**: Use the definition of morphism and properties of `flatMap` and `length`.

**Step-by-step**:

1. **Unfold the morphism application**:
   - `f •w (a :: u) = (a :: u).flatMap f` (by definition of `applyMorphism`)

2. **Simplify `flatMap` on cons**:
   - Use `List.flatMap_cons` (from Mathlib): `(a :: u).flatMap f = f a ++ u.flatMap f`
   - So `f •w (a :: u) = f a ++ (f •w u)`

3. **Apply length to both sides**:
   - `(f •w (a :: u)).length = (f a ++ (f •w u)).length`

4. **Use length of append**:
   - Use `List.length_append`: `(f a ++ (f •w u)).length = (f a).length + (f •w u).length`

5. **Conclude**: The equality holds

**Referenced lemmas**:
- `applyMorphism` (definition from `CoW/Morphism.lean`)
- `List.flatMap_cons` (from Mathlib): `(a :: l).flatMap f = f a ++ l.flatMap f`
- `List.length_append` (from Mathlib): `(l₁ ++ l₂).length = l₁.length + l₂.length`

**Concrete proof structure**:

```lean
simp only [applyMorphism]
rw [List.flatMap_cons]
exact List.length_append (f a) (u.flatMap f)
```

Or even simpler with `simp`:

```lean

```

Or most direct:

```lean
rfl  -- if simp lemmas are set up correctly
```

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
Let me analyze this theorem step-by-step.

**Goal**: Prove that the composition of two codings is a coding.

**Understanding the definitions**:

From `CoW/Morphism.lean`:
```lean
def IsCoding (f : α → Word β) : Prop :=
  ∀ a : α, (f a).length = 1

def compMorphism (g : β → Word γ) (f : α → Word β) : α → Word γ :=
  fun a => g •w (f a)
```

**What we have**:
- `hf : IsCoding f`, which means `∀ a, (f a).length = 1`
- `hg : IsCoding g`, which means `∀ b, (g b).length = 1`

**What we need to show**:
- `IsCoding (compMorphism g f)`, which means `∀ a, ((compMorphism g f) a).length = 1`

**Key observations**:

1. By definition: `(compMorphism g f) a = g •w (f a)`

2. Since `hf : IsCoding f`, we have `(f a).length = 1`, so `f a` is a single-letter word. 
   This means `f a = [b]` for some `b : β`.

3. For a single-letter word `[b]`, applying a morphism gives: `g •w [b] = g b`
   - This uses `applyMorphism_letter` from the library

4. Since `hg : IsCoding g`, we have `(g b).length = 1`

5. Therefore: `((compMorphism g f) a).length = (g •w (f a)).length = (g b).length = 1`

**Proof strategy**:

1. Unfold `IsCoding (compMorphism g f)`: need to show `∀ a, ((compMorphism g f) a).length = 1`

2. Take arbitrary `a : α`

3. Unfold `compMorphism`: `(compMorphism g f) a = g •w (f a)`

4. Since `(f a).length = 1` (from `hf`), we can write `f a = [b]` for some `b`
   - Actually, we might not need to extract the `b` explicitly
   - We can use a more direct approach

5. Use a lemma about morphism length for single elements:
   - For a coding `g`, we have `(g •w [b]).length = (g b).length = 1`
   - Or more generally, use `IsUniform.length_image` if applicable

Actually, let me think more carefully about how to get from `f a` to its structure.

**Better approach**:

From `hf a`, we know `(f a).length = 1`. 

For a list of length 1, we can extract its unique element. In Mathlib, there should be lemmas about lists of length 1, such as:
- `List.length_eq_one : l.length = 1 ↔ ∃ a, l = [a]`

So from `(f a).length = 1`, we can get `∃ b, f a = [b]`.

Then:
```lean
(compMorphism g f) a 
  = g •w (f a)
  = g •w [b]         -- by substitution
  = g b              -- by applyMorphism_letter
```

And `(g b).length = 1` by `hg b`.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
**Goal**: Prove `IsCoding (compMorphism g f)` given `IsCoding f` and `IsCoding g`.

**Strategy**: Show that for each letter, the composition produces a word of length 1.

   - So `g •w [b] = g b`
   - Goal becomes: `(g b).length = 1`

7. **Apply coding property of g**:
   - Use `hg b : (g b).length = 1`
   - This directly proves the goal

- `compMorphism` (definition from `CoW/Morphism.lean`)

```lean
-- Now: List.flatMap g [b].length = 1
```

**Goal**: Prove that the composition of two uniform morphisms is uniform, with the length being the product of the individual lengths.

```lean
def IsUniform (f : α → Word β) (k : ℕ) : Prop :=
  ∀ a : α, (f a).length = k

def compMorphism (g : β → Word γ) (f : α → Word β) : α → Word γ :=
  fun a => g •w (f a)
```

Also from the library:
```lean
lemma IsUniform.length_image {f : α → Word β} {k : ℕ}
    (hf : IsUniform f k) (w : Word α) :
    (f •w w).length = w.length * k
```

**What we have**:
- `hf : IsUniform f j`, which means `∀ a, (f a).length = j`
- `hg : IsUniform g k`, which means `∀ b, (g b).length = k`

**What we need to show**:
- `IsUniform (compMorphism g f) (j * k)`, which means `∀ a, ((compMorphism g f) a).length = j * k`

**Key observations**:

1. By definition: `(compMorphism g f) a = g •w (f a)`

2. We can use `IsUniform.length_image` with `hg` to compute the length of `g •w (f a)`:
   - `(g •w (f a)).length = (f a).length * k` (by `IsUniform.length_image hg`)

3. From `hf a`, we know `(f a).length = j`

4. Therefore: `(g •w (f a)).length = j * k`

**Proof strategy**:

1. Unfold `IsUniform`: need to show `∀ a, ((compMorphism g f) a).length = j * k`

2. Take arbitrary `a : α`

3. Unfold `compMorphism`: `(compMorphism g f) a = g •w (f a)`

4. Apply `IsUniform.length_image hg` to get:
   `(g •w (f a)).length = (f a).length * k`

5. Use `hf a` to substitute `(f a).length = j`:
   `(g •w (f a)).length = j * k`

6. Done!

This proof should be quite straightforward using the existing lemmas.

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
Let me analyze this theorem step-by-step.

**Goal**: Prove that a non-erasing morphism preserves proper prefixes.

**Understanding the definitions**:

From `CoW/Morphism.lean`:
```lean
def IsNonErasing (f : α → Word β) : Prop :=
  ∀ a : α, f a ≠ []
```

From `CoW/ProperPrefix.lean`:
```lean
def IsProperPrefix (u w : Word α) : Prop := u ≤ₚ w ∧ u ≠ w

lemma IsProperPrefix.def (u w : Word α) :
    (u <ₚ w) ↔ ∃ v, w = u ++ v ∧ v ≠ []
```

From `CoW/Morphism.lean`:
```lean
lemma applyMorphism_preserves_prefix {f : α → Word β} {u w : Word α}
    (h : u ≤ₚ w) : (f •w u) ≤ₚ (f •w w)
```

**What we have**:
- `hf : IsNonErasing f`, meaning `∀ a, f a ≠ []`
- `h : u <ₚ w`, meaning `u ≤ₚ w ∧ u ≠ w`

**What we need to show**:
- `(f •w u) <ₚ (f •w w)`, meaning `(f •w u) ≤ₚ (f •w w) ∧ (f •w u) ≠ (f •w w)`

**Key observations**:

1. We already have `applyMorphism_preserves_prefix` which gives us `(f •w u) ≤ₚ (f •w w)` from `u ≤ₚ w`.

2. We need to additionally show `(f •w u) ≠ (f •w w)`.

3. From `h : u <ₚ w`, we can extract:
   - `h.1 : u ≤ₚ w` (u is a prefix of w)
   - `h.2 : u ≠ w` (u is strictly not equal to w)
   
   Or using `IsProperPrefix.def`:
   - `∃ v, w = u ++ v ∧ v ≠ []`

4. From the decomposition `w = u ++ v` with `v ≠ []`:
   - `f •w w = f •w (u ++ v) = (f •w u) ++ (f •w v)` (by morphism homomorphism)
   - We need to show `(f •w u) ≠ (f •w u) ++ (f •w v)`
   - This is true if `f •w v ≠ []`

5. To show `f •w v ≠ []` when `v ≠ []`:
   - Since `v ≠ []`, we can write `v = a :: rest` for some `a : α` and `rest : Word α`
   - Then `f •w v = f •w (a :: rest) = (f a) ++ (f •w rest)`
   - Since `hf a : f a ≠ []`, we have `f •w v ≠ []`

**Proof strategy**:

1. Extract the proper prefix decomposition: `w = u ++ v` with `v ≠ []`

2. Show `(f •w u) ≤ₚ (f •w w)` using `applyMorphism_preserves_prefix`

3. Show `(f •w u) ≠ (f •w w)` by:
   a. Showing `f •w v ≠ []` (using non-erasing property)
   b. Using that `f •w w = (f •w u) ++ (f •w v)`
   c. Concluding that equality would imply `f •w v = []`, contradiction

No specific plan block detected.

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
Looking at the Builder's proof, it's very close but there are some issues in the final steps. Let me trace through:

1. The structure is good: split into showing the prefix property and the inequality
2. The prefix part uses `applyMorphism_preserves_prefix` correctly
3. For the inequality part, the Builder:
   - Assumes `heq : f •w u = f •w w`
   - Derives that `f •w v = []`
   - Does case analysis on `v`
   - For `v = a :: rest`, shows `f a ⬝ f •w rest = []`
   - Tries to conclude `f a = []`

The issue is in the last step. The Builder tries to prove `f a = []` from `f a ⬝ f •w rest = []`, but the case analysis on `f a` might not be working as intended, or there might be a simpler way.

Actually, `f a ⬝ f •w rest = []` should directly imply `f a = []` by the property of list append:
- If `l₁ ++ l₂ = []`, then `l₁ = []` and `l₂ = []`

This is `List.append_eq_nil` in Mathlib: `l ++ l' = [] ↔ l = [] ∧ l' = []`

So instead of the case analysis on `f a`, we can just use:

```lean
have h_append_eq_nil : f a = [] ∧ f •w rest = [] := by
  simp only [Word.concat] at this
  exact List.append_eq_nil.mp this
```

Then `h_append_eq_nil.1 : f a = []` contradicts `hf a`.

Let me provide a cleaner revised plan.

- `IsProperPrefix.def` (from `CoW/ProperPrefix.lean`)
- `applyMorphism_preserves_prefix` (from `CoW/Morphism.lean`)
- `applyMorphism_concat` (from `CoW/Morphism.lean`)
- `List.append_eq_nil` (from Mathlib): `l ++ l' = [] ↔ l = [] ∧ l' = []`
- `List.exists_cons_of_ne_nil` (from Mathlib): `l ≠ [] → ∃ a l', l = a :: l'`
- `List.length_eq_zero` (from Mathlib): `l.length = 0 ↔ l = []`

**Concrete proof structure**:

```lean
constructor
· exact applyMorphism_preserves_prefix h.1
· intro heq
  obtain ⟨v, hw, hv⟩ := (IsProperPrefix.def u w).mp h
  have hw_morph : f •w w = (f •w u) ⬝ (f •w v) := by
    rw [← applyMorphism_concat, ← hw]
  rw [heq] at hw_morph
  simp only [Word.concat] at hw_morph
  have hv_empty : f •w v = [] := by
    have := congr_arg List.length hw_morph
    simp [List.length_append] at this
    exact List.length_eq_zero.mp (by omega)
  obtain ⟨a, rest, rfl⟩ := List.exists_cons_of_ne_nil hv
  simp only [applyMorphism, List.flatMap_cons] at hv_empty
  have ⟨ha, _⟩ := List.append_eq_nil.mp hv_empty
  exact hf a ha
```

This should work cleanly using the standard Mathlib lemmas.

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
This theorem is almost identical to the previous one about proper prefixes, but for proper suffixes instead.

**Goal**: Prove that a non-erasing morphism preserves proper suffixes.

**Understanding the definitions**:

From `CoW/ProperSuffix.lean`:
```lean
def IsProperSuffix (u w : Word α) : Prop := u ≤ₛ w ∧ u ≠ w

lemma IsProperSuffix.iff (u w : Word α) :
    (u <ₛ w) ↔ ∃ v, w = v ++ u ∧ v ≠ []
```

From `CoW/Morphism.lean`:
```lean
lemma applyMorphism_preserves_suffix {f : α → Word β} {u w : Word α}
    (h : u ≤ₛ w) : (f •w u) ≤ₛ (f •w w)
```

**What we have**:
- `hf : IsNonErasing f`, meaning `∀ a, f a ≠ []`
- `h : u <ₛ w`, meaning `u ≤ₛ w ∧ u ≠ w`

**What we need to show**:
- `(f •w u) <ₛ (f •w w)`, meaning `(f •w u) ≤ₛ (f •w w) ∧ (f •w u) ≠ (f •w w)`

**Proof strategy** (parallel to the prefix case):

1. Extract the proper suffix decomposition: `w = v ++ u` with `v ≠ []`

2. Show `(f •w u) ≤ₛ (f •w w)` using `applyMorphism_preserves_suffix`

3. Show `(f •w u) ≠ (f •w w)` by:
   a. Showing `f •w v ≠ []` (using non-erasing property)
   b. Using that `f •w w = (f •w v) ++ (f •w u)`
   c. Concluding that equality would imply `f •w v = []`, contradiction

The structure is essentially the same as the prefix case, just with suffix instead.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
**Goal**: Prove `(f •w u) <ₛ (f •w w)` given `IsNonErasing f` and `u <ₛ w`.

**Strategy**: Parallel to the proper prefix case, but using suffix lemmas instead.

**Step-by-step**:

1. **Split into two goals**:
   ```lean
   constructor
   ```

2. **First goal** (`(f •w u) ≤ₛ (f •w w)`):
   ```lean
   exact applyMorphism_preserves_suffix h.1
   ```

3. **Second goal** (`(f •w u) ≠ (f •w w)`):
   
   a. **Assume the contrary**: 
      ```lean
      intro heq
      ```
   
   b. **Extract proper suffix decomposition**:
      ```lean
      obtain ⟨v, hw, hv⟩ := (IsProperSuffix.iff u w).mp h
      ```
      Now we have `hw : w = v ++ u` and `hv : v ≠ []`
   
   c. **Rewrite `f •w w` using decomposition**:
      ```lean
      have hw_morph : f •w w = (f •w v) ⬝ (f •w u) := by
        rw [← applyMorphism_concat, ← hw]
      ```
   
   d. **Derive `f •w v = []`**:
      ```lean

      -- Now hw_morph : f •w u = (f •w v) ⬝ (f •w u)
      simp only [Word.concat] at hw_morph
      have hv_empty : f •w v = [] := by
        have hlen := congr_arg List.length hw_morph
        simp [List.length_append] at hlen
        have : (f •w v).length = 0 := by omega
        exact List.length_eq_zero.mp this
      ```
   
   e. **Derive contradiction from `v ≠ []`**:
      ```lean
      -- Since v ≠ [], we can write v = a :: rest
      obtain ⟨a, rest, rfl⟩ := List.exists_cons_of_ne_nil hv
      -- Now v = a :: rest
      simp only [applyMorphism, List.flatMap_cons] at hv_empty
      -- hv_empty : f a ++ (f •w rest) = []
      have ⟨ha_empty, _⟩ := List.append_eq_nil.mp hv_empty
      -- ha_empty : f a = []
      exact hf a ha_empty
      ```

**Referenced lemmas**:
- `IsProperSuffix.iff` (from `CoW/ProperSuffix.lean`): proper suffix decomposition
- `applyMorphism_preserves_suffix` (from `CoW/Morphism.lean`): morphisms preserve suffix relation
- `applyMorphism_concat` (from `CoW/Morphism.lean`): morphism of concatenation
- `List.append_eq_nil` (from Mathlib): `l ++ l' = [] ↔ l = [] ∧ l' = []`
- `List.exists_cons_of_ne_nil` (from Mathlib): `l ≠ [] → ∃ a l', l = a :: l'`
- `List.length_eq_zero` (from Mathlib): `l.length = 0 ↔ l = []`

**Concrete proof structure**:

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
Let me analyze this theorem step-by-step.

**Goal**: Prove that a coding morphism preserves borders.

**Understanding the definitions**:

From `CoW/Border.lean`:
```lean
def IsBorder (b w : Word α) : Prop := b <ₚ w ∧ b <ₛ w
```

From `CoW/Morphism.lean`:
```lean
def IsCoding (f : α → Word β) : Prop :=
  ∀ a : α, (f a).length = 1
```

Also we know:
```lean
lemma IsCoding.isNonErasing {f : α → Word β} (hf : IsCoding f) :
    IsNonErasing f
```

**What we have**:
- `hb : IsBorder b w`, which means `b <ₚ w ∧ b <ₛ w`
- `hf : IsCoding f`, which means `∀ a, (f a).length = 1`

**What we need to show**:
- `IsBorder (f •w b) (f •w w)`, which means `(f •w b) <ₚ (f •w w) ∧ (f •w b) <ₛ (f •w w)`

**Key observations**:

1. From `hb`, we have:
   - `hb.1 : b <ₚ w` (b is a proper prefix of w)
   - `hb.2 : b <ₛ w` (b is a proper suffix of w)

2. A coding is non-erasing (from `IsCoding.isNonErasing`)

3. We have theorems showing that non-erasing morphisms preserve proper prefixes and suffixes:
   - `morphism_preserves_proper_prefix_ne` (from the previous theorem)
   - `morphism_preserves_proper_suffix_ne` (from the previous theorem)

4. Therefore:
   - From `hb.1` and non-erasing property: `(f •w b) <ₚ (f •w w)`
   - From `hb.2` and non-erasing property: `(f •w b) <ₛ (f •w w)`

5. Combining these gives us `IsBorder (f •w b) (f •w w)`

**Proof strategy**:

1. Use `IsCoding.isNonErasing` to get that `f` is non-erasing

2. Apply `morphism_preserves_proper_prefix_ne` with `hb.1` to get `(f •w b) <ₚ (f •w w)`

3. Apply `morphism_preserves_proper_suffix_ne` with `hb.2` to get `(f •w b) <ₛ (f •w w)`

4. Combine using `constructor` or `⟨_, _⟩` to get `IsBorder (f •w b) (f •w w)`

This should be a very straightforward proof using the infrastructure we've built up.

```lean4
  · intro heq
    apply hb.1.2
    -- Prove b = w from b ≤ₚ w and equal lengths
    obtain ⟨v, hv⟩ := (IsPrefix.def b w).mp hb.1.1
    have h1 := IsUniform.length_image (IsCoding.isUniform hf) b
    have h2 := IsUniform.length_image (IsCoding.isUniform hf) w
    simp only [Nat.mul_one] at h1 h2
    rw [heq] at h1
    have hlen : b.length = w.length := by omega
    have hv_len : v.length = 0 := by
      have := congr_arg Word.length hv
      simp only [Word.length_concat] at this
      omega
    simp only [List.length_eq_zero.mp hv_len, List.append_nil] at hv
    exact hv.symm
· constructor
  · exact applyMorphism_preserves_suffix hb.2.1
  · intro heq
    apply hb.2.2
    -- Prove b = w from b ≤ₛ w and equal lengths
    obtain ⟨v, hv⟩ := (IsSuffix.def b w).mp hb.2.1
    have h1 := IsUniform.length_image (IsCoding.isUniform hf) b
    have h2 := IsUniform.length_image (IsCoding.isUniform hf) w
    simp only [Nat.mul_one] at h1 h2
    rw [heq] at h1
    have hlen : b.length = w.length := by omega
    have hv_len : v.length = 0 := by
      have := congr_arg Word.length hv
      simp only [Word.length_concat] at this
      omega
    simp only [List.length_eq_zero.mp hv_len, List.nil_append] at hv
    exact hv.symm
```
